<|startoftext|> Roast Turkey <endoftitle> 1 whole turkey (12 to 14 lb) <ing> 1 tbsp. Stick Butter <ing> ½ tsp. each salt and pepper <ing> ⅓ c. chopped parsley (optional) <ing> 1 c. chicken broth <ing> Garnish: fresh herbs <endofings> Heat oven to 325°F. <inst> You'll need a shallow roasting pan fitted with a rack. <inst> Remove giblets, neck and any fat from turkey body and neck cavities. <inst> Discard fat. <inst> Dry turkey inside and out with paper towels.Tie or clamp legs together. <inst> Twist wing tips under back. <inst> Brush skin with butter; sprinkle with salt, pepper and chopped parsley, if desired.Place breast side up on rack in pan. <inst> Insert a standard meat thermometer (if not using an instant-read) into center of a thigh next to body (not touching bone). <inst> Add broth to pan.Roast 3 to 3 3/4 hours, basting every 30 minutes with pan juices, adding more broth or water if pan seems dry. <inst> If breast gets too brown, cover it loosely with foil.About 2 hours before turkey should be done, untie legs so heat can penetrate body cavity.About 1 1/4 hours before turkey should be done, start checking for doneness. <inst> When thermometer inserted in thigh registers 180°F, remove turkey to a large serving platter or carving board. <inst> Let rest at least 30 minutes before serving for juicier meat and easier carving.Plan Ahead: Plan to have the turkey done about 1 hour before the rest of the meal. <inst> The turkey will stay hot for at least 1 hour, covered with foil. <endofinst>  <target:non-vegetarian> The turkey will stay hot for at least 1 hour, covered with foil. <|endoftext|>
